% Part 2 & 3
\chapter{Part 2 \& 3: Cue Cards \& Discussion Topics}

\section{Describe a city you enjoyed visiting}
\begin{ieltsprompt}
Describe a city you enjoyed visiting.
You should say:
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=2em, itemsep=2pt]
\item Where it is
\item When you visited it
\item How long you stayed there
\item What you did there
\item And explain why you enjoyed visiting it.
\end{itemize}
\end{ieltsprompt}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

Well, off the top of my head, I'd love to talk about my trip to Hoi An, which is a charming ancient town in central Vietnam. I visited there last summer with a couple of close friends right after our final exams, and we ended up staying for about five days.

To be honest, I was absolutely blown away by the atmosphere. The old town is lined with these beautiful yellow-walled houses, colourful lanterns hanging everywhere, and narrow cobblestone streets that make you feel like you've stepped back in time. During the day, we wandered around the Japanese Covered Bridge and visited some local tailor shops — Hoi An is famous for its custom-made clothing, you know. In the evenings, we'd sit by the Thu Bon River, release paper lanterns, and just soak in the peaceful vibes.

What really made the trip special, though, was the food. We tried Cao Lau, which is a noodle dish unique to Hoi An, and I must say it was out of this world. The combination of chewy noodles, crispy pork, and fresh herbs was simply unforgettable.

Come to think of it, the reason I enjoyed Hoi An so much was that it offered the perfect blend of culture, history, and relaxation. It wasn't overcrowded like some other tourist spots, and the locals were incredibly warm and welcoming. I'd go back there in a heartbeat if I had the chance.

\vspace{0.5em}
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{|>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.22\textwidth}|>{\centering\arraybackslash}p{0.22\textwidth}|>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}X|}
\hline
\rowcolor{ForumDarkBlue!10}
\textbf{Vocabulary} & \textbf{Pronunciation} & \textbf{Meaning} \\
\hline
\vocab{charming} & \textit{/ˈtʃɑː.mɪŋ/} & quyến rũ, duyên dáng \\
\vocab{blown away} & \textit{/bləʊn əˈweɪ/} & ấn tượng mạnh \\
\vocab{cobblestone} & \textit{/ˈkɒb.əl.stəʊn/} & đá cuội lát đường \\
\vocab{custom-made} & \textit{/ˈkʌs.təm meɪd/} & may đo riêng \\
\vocab{soak in} & \textit{/səʊk ɪn/} & tận hưởng, đắm mình \\
\vocab{out of this world} & \textit{/aʊt ɒv ðɪs wɜːld/} & tuyệt vời \\
\vocab{unforgettable} & \textit{/ˌʌn.fəˈɡet.ə.bəl/} & không thể quên \\
\vocab{blend of} & \textit{/blend ɒv/} & sự pha trộn \\
\vocab{in a heartbeat} & \textit{/ɪn ə ˈhɑːt.biːt/} & ngay lập tức \\
\hline
\end{tabularx}
\end{center}


\separator

\partthreeheader

\begin{ieltsquestion}
\textbf{1. What kinds of facilities do big cities have?}
\end{ieltsquestion}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

Well, big cities typically offer a wide range of public facilities such as modern hospitals, well-equipped schools, shopping malls, and efficient public transport systems like metros and bus networks. On top of that, you'd also find entertainment venues like cinemas, parks, and sports complexes. I think these are the things that really set major cities apart from smaller towns.

\vspace{0.5em}
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}

\hline
\vocab{facility} & \textit{/fəˈsɪl.ə.ti/} & cơ sở vật chất \\
\vocab{well-equipped} & \textit{/wel ɪˈkwɪpt/} & được trang bị tốt \\
\vocab{efficient} & \textit{/ɪˈfɪʃ.ənt/} & hiệu quả \\
\vocab{public transport} & \textit{/ˈpʌb.lɪk ˈtræns.pɔːt/} & giao thông công cộng \\
\vocab{entertainment venue} & \textit{/ˌen.təˈteɪn.mənt ˈven.juː/} & địa điểm giải trí \\
\vocab{sports complex} & \textit{/spɔːts ˈkɒm.pleks/} & khu liên hợp thể thao \\

\end{center}


\separator

\begin{ieltsquestion}
\textbf{2. Do you think modern cities are suitable for young people or old people?}
\end{ieltsquestion}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

I'd say modern cities tend to be more tailored to young people because they offer more job opportunities, vibrant social scenes, and faster-paced lifestyles that suit younger generations. That said, older people might struggle with the noise, pollution, and high cost of living. However, some cities are making efforts to become more elderly-friendly by improving healthcare services and creating more green spaces for relaxation.

\vspace{0.5em}

\separator

\begin{ieltsquestion}
\textbf{3. Before you travel to a city, what factors would you consider?}
\end{ieltsquestion}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

There are quite a few things I'd look into. First and foremost, I'd check the weather forecast so I can pack appropriately. I'd also research the local attractions, accommodation options, and food scene. As a student, budget is always a key concern, so I'd compare prices for flights and hostels beforehand. Safety is another important factor — I always make sure to check travel advisories before heading anywhere unfamiliar.

\vspace{0.5em}

\separator

\begin{ieltsquestion}
\textbf{4. What are the disadvantages of living in a very famous city?}
\end{ieltsquestion}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

One major downside is the exorbitant cost of living. In famous cities like Tokyo or London, rent and daily expenses can be astronomical, which puts a real strain on people's finances. Another issue is overcrowding — the streets are always congested, public transport is packed, and you rarely get any personal space. On top of that, the environmental problems like air pollution and noise can seriously affect residents' quality of life.

\vspace{0.5em}
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}

\hline

\vocab{exorbitant} & \textit{/ɪɡˈzɔː.bɪ.tənt/} & quá đắt đỏ \\
\vocab{astronomical} & \textit{/ˌæs.trəˈnɒm.ɪ.kəl/} & cực kỳ cao \\
\vocab{put a strain on} & \textit{/pʊt ə streɪn ɒn/} & gây áp lực lên \\

\separator

\begin{ieltsquestion}
\textbf{5. Do you prefer to visit well-developed cities or cities with a long history?}
\end{ieltsquestion}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

Personally, I'm more drawn to cities with a rich historical background because I find them more culturally stimulating. Wandering through ancient temples, old quarters, and historical museums gives me a deeper understanding of how people lived in the past. That's not to say modern cities aren't appealing — they have their own charm with cutting-edge architecture and world-class entertainment — but I think historical cities leave a more lasting impression on me.

\vspace{0.5em}

\separator

\begin{ieltsquestion}
\textbf{6. For those who live in cities, is it because they want to or have to?}
\end{ieltsquestion}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

I think it's a mixture of both, honestly. Many young people, including myself, move to cities willingly because of better educational institutions and career prospects. However, there are also people who don't really have a choice — they relocate for work because their hometown simply doesn't offer the same employment opportunities. In some cases, people are born in cities and have never known any other way of life, so it's more of a default than a deliberate choice.

\vspace{0.5em}

\vocab{educational institution} & \textit{/ˌedʒ.ʊˈkeɪ.ʃən.əl ˌɪn.stɪˈtjuː.ʃən/} & cơ sở giáo dục \\

\separator

\section{Describe a person who likes to look after the natural world}
\begin{ieltsprompt}
Describe a person who likes to look after the natural world.
You should say:
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=2em, itemsep=2pt]
\item Who this person is
\item What he or she does
\item How he or she does it
\item How often he or she does it
\item And explain how you feel about this person.
\end{itemize}
\end{ieltsprompt}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

I'd like to talk about my biology teacher, Ms. Lan, who is genuinely passionate about protecting the environment. She's been teaching at my school for over ten years, and what sets her apart from other teachers is her hands-on approach to environmental education.

Well, to be honest, she doesn't just talk about sustainability in the classroom — she actually practises what she preaches. Every month, she organises beach clean-up campaigns where she takes students to nearby coastal areas to collect plastic waste and raise awareness about marine pollution. She also maintains a community garden at the school where students learn to grow organic vegetables without using harmful pesticides.

Come to think of it, what I admire most about her is her consistency. Rain or shine, she never misses a single clean-up event. She even spends her weekends volunteering at a local wildlife rescue centre, helping to rehabilitate injured birds and turtles.

I have tremendous respect for Ms. Lan because she's living proof that one individual can make a meaningful difference. She's inspired me and many of my classmates to be more mindful of our environmental footprint, and I think that kind of influence is truly invaluable.

\vspace{0.5em}
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{|>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.22\textwidth}|>{\centering\arraybackslash}p{0.22\textwidth}|>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}X|}
\hline
\rowcolor{ForumDarkBlue!10}
\textbf{Vocabulary} & \textbf{Pronunciation} & \textbf{Meaning} \\
\hline
\vocab{passionate about} & \textit{/ˈpæʃ.ən.ət əˈbaʊt/} & đam mê về \\
\vocab{hands-on approach} & \textit{/hændz ɒn əˈprəʊtʃ/} & cách tiếp cận thực hành \\
\vocab{sustainability} & \textit{/səˌsteɪ.nəˈbɪl.ə.ti/} & sự bền vững \\
\vocab{practise what one preaches} & \textit{/ˈpræk.tɪs wɒt wʌn priːtʃɪz/} & làm đúng những gì mình nói \\
\vocab{marine pollution} & \textit{/məˈriːn pəˈluː.ʃən/} & ô nhiễm biển \\
\vocab{organic} & \textit{/ɔːˈɡæn.ɪk/} & hữu cơ \\
\vocab{rehabilitate} & \textit{/ˌriː.həˈbɪl.ɪ.teɪt/} & phục hồi \\
\vocab{environmental footprint} & \textit{/ɪnˌvaɪ.rənˈmen.təl ˈfʊt.prɪnt/} & dấu chân môi trường \\
\vocab{invaluable} & \textit{/ɪnˈvæl.jʊ.ə.bəl/} & vô giá \\
\hline
\end{tabularx}
\end{center}


\separator

\partthreeheader

\begin{ieltsquestion}
\textbf{1. Do you think parents should teach their children how to protect the environment?}
\end{ieltsquestion}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

Absolutely. I believe environmental awareness should start at home because children tend to model their parents' behaviour. Simple habits like separating waste, saving water, and reducing plastic use can be instilled from an early age. If parents lead by example, their children are far more likely to grow into environmentally responsible adults.

\vspace{0.5em}
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{|>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.22\textwidth}|>{\centering\arraybackslash}p{0.22\textwidth}|>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}X|}
\hline
\rowcolor{ForumDarkBlue!10}
\textbf{Vocabulary} & \textbf{Pronunciation} & \textbf{Meaning} \\
\hline
\vocab{environmental awareness} & \textit{/ɪnˌvaɪ.rənˈmen.təl əˈweə.nəs/} & nhận thức về môi trường \\
\vocab{model behaviour} & \textit{/ˈmɒd.əl bɪˈheɪ.vjər/} & noi theo hành vi \\
\vocab{separate waste} & \textit{/ˈsep.ər.eɪt weɪst/} & phân loại rác \\
\vocab{instil} & \textit{/ɪnˈstɪl/} & truyền dạy, thấm nhuần \\
\vocab{lead by example} & \textit{/liːd baɪ ɪɡˈzɑːm.pəl/} & làm gương \\
\vocab{environmentally responsible} & \textit{/ɪnˌvaɪ.rənˈmen.təl.i rɪˈspɒn.sə.bəl/} & có trách nhiệm với môi trường \\
\vocab{reduce} & \textit{/rɪˈdjuːs/} & giảm thiểu \\
\vocab{from an early age} & \textit{/frɒm ən ˈɜː.li eɪdʒ/} & từ nhỏ \\
\hline
\end{tabularx}
\end{center}


\separator

\begin{ieltsquestion}
\textbf{2. What laws about the environment are effective in your country?}
\end{ieltsquestion}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

In Vietnam, there have been some recent regulations aimed at cutting down on single-use plastics, which have shown promising results. Many supermarkets now charge for plastic bags, and some cities have banned Styrofoam food containers. However, I feel enforcement is still inconsistent, especially in rural areas. Overall, the legal framework is improving, but there's still a long way to go.

\vspace{0.5em}
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}

\hline
\vocab{regulation} & \textit{/ˌreɡ.jəˈleɪ.ʃən/} & quy định \\
\vocab{cut down on} & \textit{/kʌt daʊn ɒn/} & cắt giảm \\
\vocab{single-use} & \textit{/ˌsɪŋ.ɡəl ˈjuːs/} & dùng một lần \\
\vocab{promising results} & \textit{/ˈprɒm.ɪ.sɪŋ rɪˈzʌlts/} & kết quả khả quan \\
\vocab{ban} & \textit{/bæn/} & cấm \\

\vocab{legal framework} & \textit{/ˈliː.ɡəl ˈfreɪm.wɜːk/} & khung pháp lý \\
\hline
\end{tabularx}
\end{center}


\separator

\begin{ieltsquestion}
\textbf{3. Which do you think people prefer, rewards or punishment, when it comes to government intervention in environmental protection?}
\end{ieltsquestion}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

I think most people respond better to incentives rather than penalties. For instance, tax breaks for companies that adopt green practices tend to be more effective than simply imposing fines. When people feel they're being rewarded for doing the right thing, they're naturally more motivated. That said, some level of punishment is still necessary for serious offenders like factories that dump toxic waste illegally.

\vspace{0.5em}
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{|>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.22\textwidth}|>{\centering\arraybackslash}p{0.22\textwidth}|>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}X|}
\hline
\rowcolor{ForumDarkBlue!10}
\textbf{Vocabulary} & \textbf{Pronunciation} & \textbf{Meaning} \\
\hline
\vocab{incentive} & \textit{/ɪnˈsen.tɪv/} & khuyến khích, ưu đãi \\
\vocab{penalty} & \textit{/ˈpen.əl.ti/} & hình phạt \\
\vocab{tax break} & \textit{/tæks breɪk/} & ưu đãi thuế \\
\vocab{adopt} & \textit{/əˈdɒpt/} & áp dụng \\
\vocab{green practices} & \textit{/ɡriːn ˈpræk.tɪ.sɪz/} & thực hành xanh \\
\vocab{impose fines} & \textit{/ɪmˈpəʊz faɪnz/} & áp phạt \\
\vocab{motivated} & \textit{/ˈməʊ.tɪ.veɪ.tɪd/} & có động lực \\
\vocab{dump toxic waste} & \textit{/dʌmp ˈtɒk.sɪk weɪst/} & xả thải độc hại \\

\end{tabularx}
\end{center}


\separator

\section{Describe a short-term job you want to have in a foreign country}
\begin{ieltsprompt}
Describe a short-term job you want to have in a foreign country.
You should say:
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=2em, itemsep=2pt]
\item Where it is
\item How you know of it
\item What the job is
\item And explain why you want to do it.
\end{itemize}
\end{ieltsprompt}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

If I had the chance, I'd love to work as a barista at a specialty coffee shop in Melbourne, Australia, for about three to six months. I first learned about this opportunity through a gap-year travel blog that I follow on Instagram, and I've been dreaming about it ever since.

To be honest, Melbourne has this incredible café culture that's famous worldwide. The city is packed with independent coffee shops that take their craft really seriously — from hand-poured pour-overs to latte art competitions. As someone who's already obsessed with coffee, I think working there would be like a masterclass in the art of brewing.

What really appeals to me is not just the work itself, but the whole experience of living abroad. I'd get to practise my English in a native-speaking environment, meet people from different cultural backgrounds, and develop transferable skills like customer service and time management. On top of that, Melbourne is known for being one of the most liveable cities in the world, so the quality of life would be fantastic.

Come to think of it, the main reason I want this job is that it would push me out of my comfort zone and give me a taste of independence before I graduate and enter the corporate world.

\vspace{0.5em}
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{|>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.22\textwidth}|>{\centering\arraybackslash}p{0.22\textwidth}|>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}X|}
\hline
\rowcolor{ForumDarkBlue!10}
\textbf{Vocabulary} & \textbf{Pronunciation} & \textbf{Meaning} \\
\hline
\vocab{barista} & \textit{/bəˈriːs.tə/} & nhân viên pha cà phê \\
\vocab{specialty} & \textit{/ˈspeʃ.əl.ti/} & đặc biệt, chuyên biệt \\
\vocab{gap year} & \textit{/ɡæp jɪər/} & năm nghỉ giữa kỳ \\
\vocab{craft} & \textit{/krɑːft/} & nghề thủ công, kỹ năng \\
\vocab{masterclass} & \textit{/ˈmɑː.stə.klɑːs/} & khóa học bậc thầy \\
\vocab{transferable skills} & \textit{/trænsˈfɜː.rə.bəl skɪlz/} & kỹ năng có thể chuyển đổi \\

\begin{ieltsquestion}

\end{ieltsquestion}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

From what I've seen, a lot of young people take up jobs in the hospitality sector, like working as hotel receptionists, tour guides, or waiters. Teaching English is another really popular option, especially in Asian countries. Some also do farm work through programs like WWOOF, which lets you work on organic farms in exchange for accommodation and meals.

\separator

\begin{ieltsquestion}
\textbf{2. What challenges do young people face when working abroad?}
\end{ieltsquestion}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

I think the biggest challenge is probably the language barrier. Even if you speak English well, understanding local slang or accents can be really tricky at first. Cultural differences are another hurdle — things like workplace etiquette, communication styles, and even sense of humour can vary dramatically. Homesickness is also a real issue, especially for those who've never been away from their families for an extended period.

\vspace{0.5em}

\separator

\section{Describe a time when you gave advice to others}
\begin{ieltsprompt}
Describe a time when you gave advice to others.
You should say:
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=2em, itemsep=2pt]
\item When it was
\item To whom you gave the advice
\item What the advice was
\item And explain why you gave the advice.
\end{itemize}
\end{ieltsprompt}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

This actually happened just a few months ago when my best friend, Minh, was stressing out about choosing his university major. He was torn between pursuing computer science, which his parents wanted, and graphic design, which was his true passion.

Well, I could see he was really struggling to make a decision, so I sat down with him over coffee and shared my perspective. I told him that while it's important to consider his parents' wishes, at the end of the day, he'd be the one spending four years studying the subject and potentially building a career around it. So my advice was to follow his passion but also do thorough research into the career prospects of graphic design — basically to show his parents that it's a viable and rewarding career path, not just a hobby.

To be honest, I gave him this advice because I had gone through a similar dilemma myself when choosing between business and fine arts. I ended up picking business, which I don't regret, but I've always wished someone had encouraged me to think more carefully about what truly makes me happy rather than just what seems practical.

In the end, Minh decided to major in graphic design, and he's absolutely thriving now. He even landed a freelance gig recently, so I'm really glad I spoke up.

\vspace{0.5em}
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{|>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.22\textwidth}|>{\centering\arraybackslash}p{0.22\textwidth}|>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}X|}
\hline
\rowcolor{ForumDarkBlue!10}
\textbf{Vocabulary} & \textbf{Pronunciation} & \textbf{Meaning} \\
\hline
\vocab{stress out} & \textit{/stres aʊt/} & căng thẳng \\
\vocab{torn between} & \textit{/tɔːn bɪˈtwiːn/} & phân vân giữa \\
\vocab{perspective} & \textit{/pəˈspek.tɪv/} & quan điểm, góc nhìn \\
\vocab{at the end of the day} & \textit{/æt ðə end ɒv ðə deɪ/} & cuối cùng thì \\
\vocab{thorough research} & \textit{/ˈθʌr.ə rɪˈsɜːtʃ/} & nghiên cứu kỹ lưỡng \\
\vocab{viable} & \textit{/ˈvaɪ.ə.bəl/} & khả thi \\
\vocab{dilemma} & \textit{/dɪˈlem.ə/} & tình thế tiến thoái lưỡng nan \\
\vocab{thrive} & \textit{/θraɪv/} & phát triển mạnh \\
\vocab{speak up} & \textit{/spiːk ʌp/} & lên tiếng \\
\hline
\end{tabularx}
\end{center}


\separator

\partthreeheader

\begin{ieltsquestion}
\textbf{1. Should people prepare before giving advice?}
\end{ieltsquestion}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

Definitely. I think good advice requires some thought and perhaps even a bit of research beforehand. If you just blurt out whatever comes to mind without considering the other person's situation thoroughly, your advice might do more harm than good. Taking the time to understand the full picture shows that you genuinely care and increases the likelihood that your advice will actually be helpful.

\vspace{0.5em}
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}

\textbf{Vocabulary} & \textbf{Pronunciation} & \textbf{Meaning} \\
\hline
\vocab{require} & \textit{/rɪˈkwaɪər/} & yêu cầu \\
\vocab{blurt out} & \textit{/blɜːt aʊt/} & buột miệng nói \\
\vocab{thoroughly} & \textit{/ˈθʌr.ə.li/} & kỹ lưỡng \\
\vocab{do more harm than good} & \textit{/duː mɔːr hɑːm ðæn ɡʊd/} & gây hại nhiều hơn lợi \\
\vocab{genuinely} & \textit{/ˈdʒen.ju.ɪn.li/} & thực sự \\
\vocab{likelihood} & \textit{/ˈlaɪ.kli.hʊd/} & khả năng \\
\vocab{the full picture} & \textit{/ðə fʊl ˈpɪk.tʃər/} & toàn cảnh \\
\vocab{beforehand} & \textit{/bɪˈfɔː.hænd/} & trước đó \\
\hline
\end{tabularx}
\end{center}


\separator

\begin{ieltsquestion}
\textbf{2. Is it good to ask advice from strangers online?}
\end{ieltsquestion}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

It can be useful in certain situations, like getting product recommendations or technical help. Online communities often have experts who are willing to share their knowledge for free. However, I'd be cautious about seeking personal or medical advice from strangers because you never know their qualifications or intentions. There's also the risk of misinformation, which can lead to poor decision-making. So I think it's fine as a starting point, but you should always verify what you read.

\vspace{0.5em}

\hline
\vocab{recommendation} & \textit{/ˌrek.ə.menˈdeɪ.ʃən/} & lời giới thiệu \\
\vocab{community} & \textit{/kəˈmjuː.nə.ti/} & cộng đồng \\
\vocab{cautious} & \textit{/ˈkɔː.ʃəs/} & thận trọng \\
\vocab{qualification} & \textit{/ˌkwɒl.ɪ.fɪˈkeɪ.ʃən/} & trình độ, bằng cấp \\
\vocab{misinformation} & \textit{/ˌmɪs.ɪn.fəˈmeɪ.ʃən/} & thông tin sai lệch \\
\vocab{decision-making} & \textit{/dɪˈsɪʒ.ən ˈmeɪ.kɪŋ/} & ra quyết định \\
\vocab{verify} & \textit{/ˈver.ɪ.faɪ/} & xác minh \\
\vocab{starting point} & \textit{/ˈstɑː.tɪŋ pɔɪnt/} & điểm khởi đầu \\

\section{Describe a person who often helps others}
\begin{ieltsprompt}
Describe a person who often helps others.
You should say:
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=2em, itemsep=2pt]
\item Who this person is
\item How this person helps others
\item How you know about this person
\item And explain why you think this person likes to help others.
\end{itemize}
\end{ieltsprompt}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

The person I'd like to describe is my class representative, Huy. He's been in my study group since our freshman year, and honestly, he's one of the most selfless people I've ever met.

What really stands out about Huy is that he goes out of his way to help classmates who are struggling academically. Before every major exam, he organises free tutoring sessions in the library where he explains complex concepts in a really approachable, easy-to-understand way. He even creates shared Google Drive folders with neatly organised notes and past exam papers. To be honest, I don't think half of our class would have passed statistics without his help.

Beyond academics, Huy is also very active in volunteer work. He coordinates blood donation drives on campus and has been mentoring underprivileged high school students on weekends for the past two years.

I think the reason Huy enjoys helping others is that he genuinely finds fulfilment in seeing people succeed. He once told me that growing up in a low-income family taught him the value of community support, and he wants to pay it forward whenever he can. That kind of empathy and generosity is quite rare among people our age, and it really inspires me to be more giving as well.

\vspace{0.5em}
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{|>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.22\textwidth}|>{\centering\arraybackslash}p{0.22\textwidth}|>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}X|}
\hline
\rowcolor{ForumDarkBlue!10}
\textbf{Vocabulary} & \textbf{Pronunciation} & \textbf{Meaning} \\
\hline
\vocab{class representative} & \textit{/klɑːs ˌrep.rɪˈzen.tə.tɪv/} & lớp trưởng \\
\vocab{selfless} & \textit{/ˈself.ləs/} & vị tha, không ích kỷ \\
\vocab{go out of one's way} & \textit{/ɡəʊ aʊt ɒv wʌnz weɪ/} & cố gắng hết sức \\
\vocab{tutoring session} & \textit{/ˈtjuː.tər.ɪŋ ˈseʃ.ən/} & buổi dạy kèm \\
\vocab{approachable} & \textit{/əˈprəʊ.tʃə.bəl/} & dễ tiếp cận \\
\vocab{blood donation drive} & \textit{/blʌd dəʊˈneɪ.ʃən draɪv/} & đợt hiến máu \\
\vocab{underprivileged} & \textit{/ˌʌn.dəˈprɪv.əl.ɪdʒd/} & thiệt thòi \\
\vocab{pay it forward} & \textit{/peɪ ɪt ˈfɔː.wəd/} & trả ơn bằng cách giúp người khác \\
\vocab{empathy} & \textit{/ˈem.pə.θi/} & sự đồng cảm \\
\hline
\end{tabularx}
\end{center}

\begin{ieltsquestion}
\textbf{1. What can children do to help their parents?}
\end{ieltsquestion}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

Children can contribute in many practical ways, even from a young age. Simple tasks like tidying up their rooms, washing the dishes, or helping with grocery shopping can make a significant difference in busy households. As they get older, they can take on more responsibility, such as cooking simple meals or looking after younger siblings. Beyond chores, even just showing appreciation and being well-behaved can really lighten the burden on parents.

\separator

\begin{ieltsquestion}
\textbf{2. Should children help their parents with household chores?}
\end{ieltsquestion}

\textbf{Sample 1: Học sinh / Sinh viên}

I strongly believe they should. Doing household chores teaches children essential life skills like time management, discipline, and a sense of responsibility. It also helps them understand that maintaining a home is a shared effort, not just the parents' job. Research actually shows that children who participate in chores from a young age tend to become more empathetic and cooperative adults. So yes, it's beneficial for everyone involved.

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=2em, itemsep=2pt]
